<div id="review_1352841696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1352841696" />
    <a title="R" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18849271-r"><img alt="R" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365895540p2/18849271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1352841696?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R" href="/user/show/18849271-r">R</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1352841696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13879515656549679184">Hey, look, someone decided to write Twilight with real vampires!<br/><br/>Okay, that’s not exactly fair. This book came out about 4 years before Twilight and there’s enough of a difference here that I would never think to call the two books carbon copies of each other. At the same time, if you only read the first few chapters of Demon in My View, you could easily think that this is just Twilight staring a stereotypical late-90’s/early-2000’s Goth chick.<br/><br/>You see, both books start with a human girl meeting a</span>
  <span id="freeText13879515656549679184" style="display:none">Hey, look, someone decided to write Twilight with real vampires!<br /><br />Okay, that’s not exactly fair. This book came out about 4 years before Twilight and there’s enough of a difference here that I would never think to call the two books carbon copies of each other. At the same time, if you only read the first few chapters of Demon in My View, you could easily think that this is just Twilight staring a stereotypical late-90’s/early-2000’s Goth chick.<br /><br />You see, both books start with a human girl meeting a vampire whom she’s instantly drawn to. Add the fact that they meet each other while attending the same high school and, yeah, it’s Twilight 2.0.<br /><br />However, when we get to the meat of the story, the actual plot is very different from Stephenie Meyer’s rather overhyped bestseller. While Twilight was just a very strange love story, this book is something darker and far more interesting.<br /><br />The basic idea is this: Jessica, our main character, has dreamed of vampires her entire life and she’s written dozens of stories about them. She’s even had one of them professionally published and her second novel is already sitting on her editor’s desk, waiting for approval. She’s developed a whole world of these creatures who she knows better than her adoptive mother. So what happens when Jessica learns that her dreams might not be dreams? What happens if the world that she’s been losing herself to for the past 17 years is, in fact, real?<br /><br />For some authors, that might be a happy thought, but for Jessica? She’s just told the world the darkest secrets of some of the most powerful vampires on the planet. Her book’s as good as a death warrant.<br /><br />Doesn’t that sound awesome? This could be a kick-ass novel, right?<br /><br />Well, it could, but it isn’t. At least, not as awesome as I pictured. You see, the novel falls prey to the same thing that so many YA novels do: teen romance. Unfortunately, I can’t get into any more details on this subject because I’m already hovering on the edge of spoiler territory and I hate spoiling novels for those who just want a good review, so I’ll leave you with this: Demon in My View is a novel that I’d recommend to anyone who likes vampires. Even if you don’t enjoy the novel’s story, there’s enough interesting ideas here to keep you entertained and thinking. It doesn’t go as dark as a hard-core vampire novel might, but it’s certainly not another Twilight. If anything, it’s another Underworld. Good enough to entertain, but not gripping enough that I'm going to search out the other books in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13879515656549679184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_867949812" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/867949812" />
    <a title="Rants and Bants" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24862580-rants-and-bants"><img alt="Rants and Bants" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541473603p2/24862580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/867949812?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rants and Bants" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rants and Bants" href="/user/show/24862580-rants-and-bants">Rants and Bants</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24862580-rants-and-bants?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer867949812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9372618391464394634">Nostalgia again. I remember reading this back in early high school when vamps were all the rage and when I was going through my goth/vampire phase. I’d read loads of non-Twilight vampire teen books, even before it hit hard. This was one of them. It is probably my favorite one out of series, at least out of the first three (I have a fuzzy time remembering the rest, and I definitely never finished the whole series, as there were some getting published long after I’d read the first three). It had e</span>
  <span id="freeText9372618391464394634" style="display:none">Nostalgia again. I remember reading this back in early high school when vamps were all the rage and when I was going through my goth/vampire phase. I’d read loads of non-Twilight vampire teen books, even before it hit hard. This was one of them. It is probably my favorite one out of series, at least out of the first three (I have a fuzzy time remembering the rest, and I definitely never finished the whole series, as there were some getting published long after I’d read the first three). It had even inspired me in some ways to start a vampire story myself which I never got around to finishing, but maybe one day…maybe one day…<br /><br />As an adult, it was still somewhat enjoyable, but it didn’t impress me as much as a teen. I didn’t feel like the characters were developed as much, nor did it have a full closure. You’re still left wondering certain things. The protagonist, Jessica, is not very likeable. But she isn’t the worst, by any means. The thing I like about this series is that it focuses on the same world but different characters in each book. So if you don’t like the ones in here (or in any of them) you won’t have to worry about sitting through their perspectives in the next book. One last criticism is about Jessica’s success with publishing…of course as a naïve teenager who wanted to be a writer, I thought it was awesome that it was as simple as, she wrote for hours on end for a full weekend, then got it published like <i>that</i>. At such a young age, making money already, AND getting the bonus of being able to stay anonymous. And...getting to see her world come to life, literally (albeit in a horrifying way). Now of course I realize that that’s not how it work (the quick-publishing part) XD It’s very unrealistic. I guess these were unique circumstances, but still.<br /><br />In my opinion this is still a fun little series to read and I will be continuing it and reviewing all of the <i>Den of Shadows</i> books on here. I think they would be more enjoyable for specifically teens or pre-teens though.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9372618391464394634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('MyGu+KHZLAjC30wGd+IgoLtYe3rVNbZkUzSLLGvXD1u2tkRQd4+pQdjkm+AkedVSTU0DY2AaqJGNA2Ycqie+hA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YoYmA2V+gheXPjugC0P4fydUCO04fA9fCPC/tMjY6Y7nEcyrsygHXo0F7EZY2A2N0UFw9I1TEarWx1KECShYUQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4846431755733005500">I grew up in Concord, Massachusetts, where I matriculated through the public Concord-Carlisle school district from kindergarten until my graduation in 2001. The best part of school, from fifth grade until the year I graduated, was definitely chorus. I love music, and I love to sing, and though I never had the courage or the talent to participate in any of the high school plays as a performer, I en</span>
  <span id="freeText4846431755733005500" style="display:none">I grew up in Concord, Massachusetts, where I matriculated through the public Concord-Carlisle school district from kindergarten until my graduation in 2001. The best part of school, from fifth grade until the year I graduated, was definitely chorus. I love music, and I love to sing, and though I never had the courage or the talent to participate in any of the high school plays as a performer, I enjoyed being involved at other levels; the music and drama community at CCHS was the highlight of my high school career. I was also on the fencing team for two years, an experience that actually inspired a couple storylines, and regret that I did not continue with that sport.<br /><br />I now live in Massachusetts with several pets... as well as, of course, my family. I am a student at the University of Massachusetts, with an English/psychology double-major. I hope to work either as an English teacher at the secondary level, or in special education. I have strong opinions about literacy, education, and how our educational systems are treated- strong enough that most of my friends know not to get me started on the subject.<br /><br />My non-writing hobbies are eclectic, and cover everything from rather domestic pastimes like cross-stitch and cooking to aquarium keeping, playing piano, gardening, carpentry, Harley-Davidsons, driving, and arguing- there are few things I enjoy more than a good debate with someone who knows how to argue, which might have something to do with a best friend who works in politics. I love to learn, so if I have down-time and nothing to do, it is not at all unusual to find me pouring over some book, website or video designed to teach me some new skill, from belly dancing (something I desperately want to learn but have not yet been brave enough to sign up for classes on) to JavaScript.</span>
